                    "text": "# The Weight of Eternity\n\nThe silence that preceded the end of all things was not a silence at all. It was the held breath of a universe that had not yet learned to scream.\n\nHigh Chancellor Meridian of the Celestial Concordance stood in the war chamber of the Citadel of Final Light, his twenty-seven arms folded across his crystalline chest in what his species recognized as deepest contemplation. Around him, the holographic displays showed the death of everything they had ever known. Galaxy after galaxy. Dimension after dimension. Reality after reality. All falling. All bowing. All kneeling before a single name that had become synonymous with absolute, unchallenged dominion.\n\nGodric.\n\nThe name itself felt wrong in the mind. Too simple. Too human. And yet the being who bore it had, in the span of two decades, done what no cosmic horror, no eldritch entity, no primordial force had ever accomplished. He had united the omniverse under a single throne. Not through negotiation. Not through alliance. Through the kind of overwhelming, incomprehensible power that made the Old Ones weep in their sleeping prisons and caused the gods themselves to invent new forms of prayer.\n\n\"Show me again,\" Meridian commanded, his voice a chime of breaking glass.\n\nThe displays shifted. They showed the feed from the outer perimeter sensors, capturing the approach vector of five small vessels. No. Not vessels. Figures. Five humanoid shapes moving through the void of space without ships, without suits, without any visible means of propulsion. They simply walked through the vacuum as though it were a pleasant meadow, their boots finding purchase on nothing at all.\n\n\"Five of them,\" whispered Sub-Strategist Vell, her bioluminescent skin pulsing with fear-colors. \"They only ever send five.\"\n\n\"And they only ever need five,\" Meridian finished. The mathematics of their situation had been calculated seventeen trillion times by the Concordance's most advanced quantum intellects. The result never changed. Absolute zero probability of successful resistance. The numbers did not care about their trillion-year history. The numbers did not care about their accumulated wisdom, their technological singularity, their mastery over the fundamental forces of creation. The numbers only cared about the arithmetic of impossibility.\n\nThe five figures stopped at the exact boundary of the Concordance's defensive perimeter. One of them raised a hand in greeting. The gesture was almost apologetic.\n\n---\n\nTen thousand years before this moment, in a kingdom whose name had been erased from every history, there had been a garden.\n\nThe garden belonged to the royal palace of Olympus, and in it, a forty-five-year-old king was failing miserably at braiding his daughter's hair.\n\n\"Father, you're pulling too hard,\" Isabel complained, though her tone carried more affection than genuine protest. She sat on a marble bench beneath an ancient olive tree, her wedding dress pooling around her like a cloud given physical form. Twenty-two years old, with her mother's dark eyes and her father's stubborn chin, she was the very image of youthful joy.\n\nGodric's thick fingers, more accustomed to gripping sword hilts and signing decrees, fumbled with the intricate golden strands. His brow furrowed in concentration, the salt-and-pepper of his close-trimmed beard catching the afternoon sunlight. The muscles of his forearms, visible beneath the rolled sleeves of his ceremonial tunic, shifted as he worked\u2014a physique maintained not through vanity but through the simple fact that a king who could not lift a boulder could not protect his people from the giants that still roamed the northern wastes.\n\n\"Hush now,\" he murmured, his deep voice carrying the particular gentleness that only his daughters ever heard. \"Your mother braided her own hair on our wedding day, and I'll not have you looking less beautiful than she did.\"\n\n\"You're comparing me to Mother on her wedding day?\" Isabel laughed. \"Father, that's a battle you've already lost.\"\n\nFrom across the garden, Reina looked up from where she was adjusting fifteen-year-old Hebe's flower crown. The queen's silver-streaked hair framed a face that time had touched with grace rather than cruelty. \"I heard that, Isabel. And for the record, your father couldn't braid my hair either. I had to redo it myself before the ceremony.\"\n\n\"You're supposed to be on my side,\" Godric called to his wife, the mock indignation in his voice undermined by the warmth that softened every line of his face.\n\n\"The king has no allies on the battlefield of daughters,\" Reina replied serenely. \"Thorin taught me that.\"\n\nAs if summoned by his name, the court wizard appeared at the garden's entrance. Thorin was a man of sixty-three winters, his long white beard tucked into his belt to prevent it from tangling in his spell components, his robes a deep blue embroidered with silver constellations. Behind him, the spires of Olympus rose against a sky so perfectly clear it seemed painted by divine hands.\n\n\"Your Majesty, the guests are assembled. The high priest is ready.\" Thorin's voice carried the particular cadence of a man who had served three generations of kings and found genuine joy in his service. His family had stood beside the throne of Olympus for longer than most civilizations had existed. His great-great-grandfather had served Godric's great-great-grandfather, and his son would one day serve Isabel's son. This was the way of things. This was the foundation upon which Olympus had stood for millennia.\n\nGodric finished the braid\u2014or what could charitably be called a braid\u2014and stepped back to admire his work. It was lopsided. Several strands had already escaped. Hebe was trying very hard not to giggle.\n\n\"Perfect,\" Godric declared.\n\n\"It's terrible,\" Isabel said, but she was smiling, and when she stood to embrace her father, she held him tight enough that he could feel the rapid flutter of her heart against his chest. \"Thank you, Father. For everything.\"\n\n\"For everything,\" Godric repeated softly, and for a moment, the king of Olympus was simply a father holding his daughter on her wedding day. \"You deserve the world, my star. I'm sorry I could only give you a kingdom.\"\n\n\"You gave me a family,\" Isabel whispered. \"That's more than any world.\"\n\nHe released her reluctantly, stepping back so Reina could work her maternal magic on the braid. Thorin caught his eye and nodded toward the palace, the message clear: it was time.\n\nThe kingdom of Olympus had known peace for three hundred years. Its borders were secure. Its people prospered. The neighboring kingdoms, including the ambitious Thronegate to the east, had long accepted Olympus's supremacy through a combination of diplomatic marriages, mutually beneficial trade agreements, and the unspoken acknowledgment that challenging the Olympian military was an exercise in creative suicide. Godric had spent his reign cultivating this peace, believing\u2014perhaps naively\u2014that the horrors of his grandfather's wars would never need to be repeated.\n\nHe believed this right up until the moment the first fireball struck the wedding hall.\n\n---\n\nThe ceremony had been beautiful. Isabel had walked down the aisle on Godric's arm, her repaired braid gleaming, her groom\u2014a young duke from the southern provinces\u2014weeping openly at the sight of her. The vows had been spoken. The priest had raised his hands to pronounce them wed.\n\nAnd then the sky had opened.\n\nThe Thronegate forces did not announce themselves. There was no declaration of war, no ultimatum, no opportunity for surrender. One moment, the wedding hall was filled with the soft glow of candlelight and the murmured blessings of four hundred guests. The next, the ceiling was gone, replaced by a maw of fire and screaming metal.\n\nGodric's first instinct was to shield his family. His body moved before his mind could process, throwing himself across Isabel and Reina as burning debris rained down. Hebe was shrieking somewhere to his left. The groom was already dead, a shard of enchanted steel protruding from his chest.\n\n\"THORIN!\" Godric roared. \"THE QUEEN! GET THE QUEEN!\"\n\nBut there was no reaching anyone. The attack was systematic, devastating, designed not for conquest but for annihilation. Dragons descended from the smoke-choked sky, their riders raining destruction on the palace grounds. Soldiers in Thronegate colors poured through breaches in the walls. The Olympian guard fought back with the desperate courage of men who knew they were already dead, buying seconds with their lives.\n\nGodric drew the ceremonial sword at his hip\u2014not his battle blade, just a decorative piece meant to look impressive during formal occasions\u2014and killed the first Thronegate soldier to reach his family. Then the second. Then the third. His body remembered the wars of his youth. His muscles followed patterns drilled into them decades ago. But there were too many. There were always too many.\n\n\"Godric!\" Reina's voice cut through the chaos. She had Hebe clutched against her chest, one hand pressed to a wound in her side where a piece of debris had struck her. Blood stained her silver dress black in the firelight. \"Isabel\u2014\"\n\nHe turned. He saw his eldest daughter pinned beneath a fallen pillar, her wedding dress now more red than white, her eyes still open, still aware, still fixed on her father's face.\n\n\"Father,\" she said. Or tried to say. The word came out as a bubble of blood.\n\nThe world stopped.\n\nGodric had known battle. He had watched men die. He had killed men. But this\u2014this was not battle. This was the negation of everything he had ever loved, compressed into a single, endless moment of watching his daughter's eyes go still.\n\nA hand grabbed his shoulder. Thorin. The wizard's face was streaked with soot and tears, his robes torn, blood flowing from a gash across his scalp. In his free hand, he was tracing symbols in the air that burned with azure fire.\n\n\"Your Majesty, I can save you. There's a spell\u2014my bloodline\u2014a sanctuary\u2014\"\n\n\"I'm not leaving them,\" Godric snarled, trying to pull away. Reina had collapsed now, her hand still reaching for Isabel even as her own life faded. Hebe was silent, her small body limp in her mother's arms.\n\n\"You're not leaving them. You're avenging them.\" Thorin's voice cracked with the weight of what he was about to do. \"My ancestors forbid this spell for a reason, but they never foresaw this. They never\u2014\"\n\nA blade erupted through Thorin's chest from behind. The wizard's eyes widened, his mouth forming a perfect O of surprise. The symbols he had been tracing flared once, brilliant white, and then everything collapsed into light.\n\nThe spell, incomplete. The intention, preserved. The caster, dying even as the magic took hold.\n\nGodric felt reality tear around him. He felt himself being pulled sideways through dimensions that had no names, through spaces that existed between the spaces that existed. The last thing he saw of Olympus\u2014of his kingdom, his family, his world\u2014was Thronegate soldiers standing over the bodies of his wife and daughters, laughing.\n\nThen there was darkness.\n\nAnd then there was nothing.\n\nAnd then, in the nothing, something began to change.\n\n---\n\nThe hidden sanctuary had been built by Thorin's ancestors in an age so distant that even the oldest dragons had forgotten its existence. It existed in a pocket dimension, a fold in reality so subtle that no god or demon had ever detected it. Its walls were lined with the accumulated magical knowledge of a hundred generations of court wizards, and at its center, suspended in a column of light that had burned continuously for over forty millennia, was the stasis field.\n\nGodric's body came to rest within that field. The incomplete teleportation spell merged with the sanctuary's ambient magic, creating a cascade reaction that no wizard had ever predicted because no wizard had ever been foolish enough to attempt what Thorin had done in his final moments.\n\nThe stasis took hold immediately. Cellular activity ceased. Neurological function paused. The biological clock that had ticked steadily for forty-five years simply... stopped. Godric's body would never age another second. His beard would never grow. His hair would never gray beyond its current salt-and-pepper. His muscles would never atrophy. He would remain, in physical terms, exactly as he was at the moment of his preservation: a forty-five-year-old king at the peak of masculine vitality, frozen in amber.\n\nBut the preservation was only the beginning.\n\nDeep within the stasis field, at a level so fundamental that it predated the existence of physics itself, something was amplifying. The spell's incomplete nature had interacted with the sanctuary's protective wards in ways that defied explanation, creating what could only be described as a perpetual engine of enhancement. Every quality that defined Godric's existence began to multiply. Not by increments. Not by percentages. By factors of one thousand, and then by themselves, and then by the product of that multiplication, repeating endlessly, perpetually, at a rate measured in the smallest units of time that reality could express.\n\nOne Planck second. Strength multiplied by one thousand. Intelligence multiplied by itself. Speed multiplied by the new result. Wisdom multiplied by that. Then the process began again, with each new value serving as the baseline for the next cycle of amplification.\n\nThis had been happening for ten seconds when the first superpower manifested. It was a simple ability by the standards of what would follow: complete molecular control over any substance within the wielder's awareness. A civilization-ending power if weaponized. A footnote in the catalog of what was to come.\n\nTen seconds later, another power emerged. Then another. Then another. Each one would have been sufficient to establish a being as the supreme deity of any pantheon. Each one was merely a single note in a symphony of omnipotence that was composing itself in the silent dark of the sanctuary.\n\nAnd yet the omniverse did not end. The stasis field did not collapse under the weight of the power it contained. The sanctuary did not detonate with the force of a billion supernovas. Because one of those first powers\u2014manifesting in the very first second of the transformation\u2014was a concealment ability so profound, so absolute, that it perfectly contained everything that would ever follow. The power to hold back. To mask. To exist without existing. And like every other ability, this concealment multiplied in potency with each passing Planck second, forever staying ahead of the infinite power it was designed to hide.\n\nTime passed. Not in the sanctuary\u2014there, time had become a suggestion rather than a law\u2014but in the universe beyond the pocket dimension. Empires rose and fell. Gods were born and died. The kingdom of Olympus faded from memory, its ruins buried beneath newer ruins, which were themselves buried beneath still newer ruins. The kingdom of Thronegate, riding the momentum of its conquest, expanded across continents, then across oceans, then\u2014as technology and magic merged into something unprecedented\u2014across their galaxy.\n\nTen thousand years passed. And in all that time, the amplification never stopped. Never paused. Never even flickered.\n\n---\n\nThe merchant ship was called the *Anna's Grace*, named for a woman who had told her husband that naming a cargo vessel after her was the least romantic thing he could possibly do, and who had then cried when she saw the name painted on the hull.\n\nBlake had been a merchant for sixteen years, ever since he'd mustered out of the planetary defense force with a bum knee, a modest pension, and a burning desire to never take orders from anyone ever again. The *Anna's Grace* was his third ship, purchased with the profits from a particularly lucrative run of medical supplies to a quarantine zone, and she was the love of his mechanical life.\n\n\"Mutton chops are not a personality,\" his wife Anna had told him that morning, as she did most mornings.\n\n\"They're a statement,\" Blake had replied, stroking the impressive growth of reddish-brown facial hair that framed his jaw. At thirty-eight, he had the sort of weathered handsomeness that came from decades of hard work and the particular stubbornness of a man who refused to concede that his forties were approaching. \"A statement that says 'I am a man of substance and character.'\"\n\n\"It says 'I am a man who doesn't own a razor.'\"\n\nTheir son Josh, twelve years old and already showing signs of his father's merchant instincts, had looked up from his breakfast. \"Dad, why don't you just shave?\"\n\n\"Because then your mother would have nothing to complain about, and she'd have to confront the existential void of a perfect marriage.\"\n\nAnna had thrown a piece of toast at him. Their eight-year-old daughter Rhea had giggled. It was, by all accounts, a perfectly ordinary morning in the Blake household.\n\nNow, three weeks later, Blake was standing in the cargo hold of his ship, staring at a wall that was not supposed to be there.\n\nThe *Anna's Grace* had been running a standard route through the Outer Arm systems, delivering terraforming equipment to a fledgling colony. A routine job. A boring job. Exactly the kind of job Blake preferred, because boring jobs didn't get you shot at by pirates or impounded by customs officials with delusions of grandeur. But a navigation glitch\u2014or what he assumed was a navigation glitch\u2014had pulled them out of hyperlight early, depositing them in an uncharted system with a damaged hyperdrive and a dwindling fuel supply.\n\nThe uncharted system contained exactly one planet. The planet contained exactly one structure, visible from orbit as a geometric anomaly in an otherwise featureless landscape. And that structure, upon closer inspection, proved to be a building of impossible architecture that radiated magical energy like heat from a dying star.\n\nBlake was not a wizard. He had never been a wizard. His family, as far back as anyone could trace, had been merchants, soldiers, farmers\u2014practical people doing practical things in a galaxy that rewarded practicality. But when he touched the wall of the structure and felt it pulse beneath his fingers like a living thing, something deep in his blood sang in recognition.\n\nHe did not know\u2014would never know\u2014that the song came from a lineage that stretched back ten thousand years, from a bloodline that had served the kings of a forgotten kingdom, from a wizard who had died casting a spell that should have been impossible. He only knew that when he pressed his palm against the cold stone, the wall opened, and a staircase spiraled down into darkness, and at the bottom of that staircase, something was waiting.\n\nThe inner chamber was vast, cathedral-like, its walls covered in glowing script that Blake's eyes could not quite focus on. And at its center, suspended in a pillar of light that hummed at a frequency felt in the bones rather than heard, was a man.\n\nHe appeared to be sleeping. Or dead. Or something in between. His physique was remarkable\u2014the kind of musculature that belonged on ancient statues depicting forgotten gods. His hair was dark, short, with precise lines of silver at the temples. His beard, neatly trimmed, showed the same distinguished salt-and-pepper pattern. He looked, Blake thought, like a king. Not a modern king\u2014the galaxy hadn't had true kings in millennia\u2014but the sort of king that existed in old stories, the kind who led armies and wrestled monsters and fathered dynasties.\n\nBlake had no reason to touch the man. Every instinct honed by sixteen years of merchant work screamed at him to back away, to seal the chamber, to pretend he had never found this place. But the song in his blood was louder than his instincts. And when his fingers brushed the man's shoulder, the pillar of light shattered.\n\nThe man opened his eyes.\n\nAnd the universe, for the first time in ten thousand years, became aware that it had a king.\n\n---\n\nGodric's omniscience did not manifest as a flood of information. It manifested as a simple, immediate knowing\u2014the way one knows their own name, their own reflection, their own heartbeat. One moment, he was suspended in the memory of fire and blood and his daughter's dying eyes. The next, he knew everything.\n\nHe knew the name of every star that had ever burned and every star that had yet to ignite. He knew the thoughts of every sentient being in every galaxy in every dimension that comprised the omniverse. He knew the history of Thronegate\u2014how it had risen from the ashes of Olympus, how it had expanded across the galaxy, how it now held dominion over more worlds than there were grains of sand on the beaches of his lost kingdom. He knew the name of the current king: Robert, twenty-two years old, a boy raised in the shadow of ancestors who had turned regicide into a family tradition.\n\nAnd he knew the man standing before him. Blake. A merchant. A father. A husband. The last living descendant of Thorin's bloodline, though the lineage had grown so diluted over ten millennia that no genealogist in the galaxy could have traced it. Blake himself had no idea of his heritage. He had grown up in a trading family on a backwater world, had never once suspected that his ancestors had once stood beside thrones and shaped the destinies of nations.\n\nAll of this, Godric knew.\n\nAll of this, and so much more.\n\n\"Where am I?\" Blake asked, his voice steady despite the impossibility of what he was witnessing. This was a man, Godric understood, who had faced down pirates and customs agents and the occasional tax auditor. A glowing man appearing from a pillar of light was unusual, but the galaxy was full of unusual things. Merchants learned to adapt.\n\n\"You are in the sanctuary of the Olympian court wizards,\" Godric replied. His voice, after ten thousand years of silence, emerged as a resonant baritone that carried the weight of his amplification. \"You are the one who woke me. What is your name?\"\n\n\"Blake. Captain of the *Anna's Grace*.\" A pause. \"Are you... okay? You've been in that light thing for a while, I'm guessing.\"\n\nGodric almost smiled. Almost. The warmth that had once come so naturally to him flickered somewhere deep in his chest, but it could not reach the surface. The surface was still covered in the ashes of his family. \"Longer than you can imagine, Blake. But I am... functional. And I have a message that needs to be delivered.\"\n\n\"A message?\"\n\n\"Yes. To King Robert of Thronegate.\" The name tasted like poison on Godric's tongue, but his voice remained perfectly level. \"Tell him that the true King of Olympus has returned. Tell him that I challenge his right to rule. Tell him that in three days, I will face his entire military\u2014every soldier, every weapon, every dragon, every mage\u2014and I will defeat them. And when I have done so, he will abdicate his throne, or I will take it from his cooling hands.\"\n\nBlake stared at him. His merchant's mind, trained to calculate odds and assess risks, was clearly struggling with the sheer scale of what he was hearing. \"That's... a big ask for someone who just woke up from a magic nap. You know Thronegate has the largest military in the galaxy, right? They've got super-soldiers. Robot armies. Dragons that can eat continents.\"\n\n\"I know.\"\n\n\"And you want to fight all of them? By yourself?\"\n\n\"I will not fight them,\" Godric corrected. \"I will simply... end them. There is a difference.\"\n\nThe casual certainty in his voice was more terrifying than any threat could have been. Blake, who had spent his adult life learning to read people, heard no boast in those words. No bluster. No false confidence. Just a statement of fact, delivered with the same tone one might use to announce that water was wet or space was cold.\n\n\"Okay,\" Blake said slowly. \"Okay. I can... I can deliver a message, I guess. But how do I explain this to my wife?\"\n\n\"She will believe you,\" Godric said, because he knew she would, because he knew everything. \"And she will be frightened. That is acceptable. Fear is a rational response to what is about to happen.\"\n\n---\n\nKing Robert of Thronegate received the message with the particular disdain that twenty-two-year-old monarchs who had never known true hardship reserved for anything they considered beneath their attention. His throne room was a monument to Thronegate's galactic supremacy\u2014walls of living crystal that shifted through every color in the spectrum, floors of polished obsidian that reflected the constellations visible through the transparent ceiling, and a throne carved from the fused bones of the last great space dragon that had dared challenge Thronegate's dominion.\n\n\"A merchant brought this message?\" Robert asked, holding the holographic recording that Blake had reluctantly agreed to deliver. \"A merchant from some backwater trading route claims to speak for a king of a kingdom that doesn't exist?\"\n\nGeneral Aldrich, commander of Thronegate's military forces, shifted his weight. At fifty-seven, he was old enough to remember a time before Thronegate's absolute supremacy, and that memory made him more cautious than his king. \"The merchant's ship does have some unusual energy signatures. And the message itself... the language used is archaic. Pre-Thronegate. Possibly even pre-Expansion era.\"\n\n\"So?\"\n\n\"So it might be worth investigating. Before we dismiss it entirely.\"\n\nRobert waved a dismissive hand. His crown\u2014a circlet of compressed neutronium that symbolized his absolute authority\u2014glinted in the shifting light. \"Fine. Investigate. But whatever this is, it's not a threat. No one can challenge the Thronegate military. We have billions of super-soldiers. We have the mightiest magical corps in galactic history. We have robot armies that can disassemble planets. We have dragons that can breathe novas. We have ninjas so fast they experience time backwards.\" He leaned forward, his young face hardening into an expression he had practiced in mirrors since childhood. \"Whoever this 'Godric' thinks he is, he's about to learn what happens to those who challenge Thronegate.\"\n\nBut General Aldrich, whose instincts had kept him alive through three wars and seventeen assassination attempts, did not share his king's confidence. He ordered the military to maximum readiness. He deployed scouts to the coordinates where the *Anna's Grace* had been intercepted. He prepared for every contingency he could imagine.\n\nIt would not be enough.\n\nIt could never have been enough.\n\n---\n\nThe plain of Calaxis was the largest uninhabited landmass on the Thronegate homeworld, a continent-sized stretch of volcanic rock and ancient impact craters that had been used for military exercises for thousands of years. On the morning of the confrontation, it held the entire assembled might of the Thronegate military.\n\nThe numbers defied comprehension. Three billion super-soldiers, each one genetically enhanced to the point where they could punch through starship hulls and survive in hard vacuum. Two billion combat robots, ranging from human-sized infiltrator units to continent-class annihilation platforms. Five hundred thousand battle mages, each capable of leveling cities with a gesture. Fifty thousand dragons, their scales shimmering with absorbed starlight, their breaths hot enough to ignite fusion reactions. And the ninjas\u2014the legendary Shadow Corps, whose members had mastered temporal manipulation to such a degree that they experienced combat in reverse, seeing the effects of their strikes before they launched them.\n\nThronegate had never assembled this much force in one place. It had never needed to. The deployment alone had required a logistical effort that would have bankrupted a lesser civilization. But General Aldrich had insisted, and King Robert, despite his dismissive attitude, had ultimately agreed. Better, he had said, to make an example of this so-called king. Better to show the galaxy what happened to those who challenged Thronegate.\n\nGodric walked onto the plain alone.\n\nHe wore no armor. He carried no weapons. He had not aged a day from the moment the stasis took him, and the king who faced the assembled might of a galactic empire was physically identical to the king who had failed to braid his daughter's hair ten thousand years ago. The same close-cropped hair with its distinguished silvering at the temples. The same neatly trimmed salt-and-pepper beard. The same powerful physique, muscles moving beneath his simple tunic with the fluid grace of restrained power.\n\nBlake and Anna watched from a hillside three miles away, at what they believed was a safe distance. Anna was clutching her husband's arm hard enough to bruise. Her face was pale beneath her trader's tan, and she kept repeating a prayer she had learned as a child on her homeworld, a prayer to a god she had stopped believing in decades ago.\n\n\"This is insane,\" she whispered. \"This is completely insane. He's going to die. We're going to die. The whole planet is going to\u2014\"\n\n\"Shh,\" Blake said. His eyes were fixed on the distant figure of Godric, standing alone against an ocean of military might. \"Just watch.\"\n\n\"What am I watching for? A slaughter?\"\n\n\"No,\" Blake said slowly. The song in his blood was louder now, a resonant hum that seemed to vibrate in time with something vast and ancient. \"A demonstration.\"\n\nThe generals of Thronegate, observing from their command ships in low orbit, gave the order to attack. The robot armies moved first\u2014a wave of metal and energy weapons that would have overwhelmed any conventional defense in seconds. Behind them came the super-soldiers, their enhanced bodies moving at speeds that created sonic booms with every step. Above them wheeled the dragons, their riders ready to unleash continent-shattering breath weapons. And weaving through the chaos, invisible to sensors and eyes alike, came the Shadow Corps, already striking in a time-frame that should have been impossible to counter.\n\nGodric did not move.\n\nHe did not raise his hands. He did not speak a word of power. He did not even shift his stance. He simply stood there, his expression one of mild contemplation, as if he were considering what to have for lunch.\n\nThe first wave of robots reached him\u2014and ceased to exist.\n\nIt was not that they were destroyed. Destruction implied a process, a transition from whole to broken, from functional to ruined. This was something else entirely. The robots simply stopped being. One moment they were there, their weapon arrays locking onto their target. The next, they were gone, erased so completely that not even subatomic particles remained to mark their passing.\n\nThe super-soldiers fared no better. Their enhanced bodies, capable of surviving atmospheric re-entry and weapons that could crack continental plates, unraveled like smoke in a hurricane. The energy that comprised their very existence\u2014the chemical bonds of their molecules, the electrical impulses of their nervous systems, the quantum information that defined their consciousness\u2014all of it simply... stopped. In perfect, absolute silence.\n\nThe dragons fell from the sky like extinguished stars, their immense bodies winking out of existence as if they had never been real at all. Their riders, still in their saddles, dissolved into nothing before they could even register their mounts' disappearance.\n\nThe Shadow Corps experienced something worse. Their temporal manipulation abilities, which allowed them to perceive and affect events in reverse, gave them a unique perspective on their own annihilation. They experienced the ending before the beginning. They felt themselves unmade in a direction that their minds had not evolved to process. Their final moments\u2014or first moments, depending on one's temporal frame of reference\u2014were filled with a horror so profound that it transcended language, that it registered as pure, undiluted existential terror.\n\nAnd the mages\u2014the most powerful magical beings in the galaxy, each one a walking arsenal of reality-altering power\u2014felt their connection to magic itself sever. Not slowly. Not through any countering spell. The magic simply refused to acknowledge their existence anymore. Their carefully woven defensive wards collapsed not because they were broken, but because they forgot they had ever been cast. Their offensive spells fizzled into nothing because the universe no longer recognized their authority to command it.\n\nThirty seconds.\n\nThat was how long it took for the greatest military force ever assembled to cease to be.\n\nThirty seconds, and Godric had not moved a single muscle. Had not spoken. Had not even blinked.\n\nFrom the command ships in orbit, General Aldrich watched his entire career, his entire civilization's military tradition, his entire understanding of how the universe worked, vanish in less time than it took to brew a cup of tea. His tactical displays showed nothing but empty space where billions of soldiers had stood moments before. His communication channels were silent, because there was no one left to communicate with. His sensor officers were weeping, and he did not have the presence of mind to reprimand them.\n\nKing Robert, watching from his palace through a holographic feed, soiled himself. He was twenty-two years old, and he had just watched his civilization's invincibility become a joke. He was twenty-two years old, and he knew, with absolute certainty, that he was going to die.\n\n\"Bring me more wine,\" he croaked to a servant who was no longer in the room, who had fled the moment the feed began showing the impossible. \"Bring me... bring me...\"\n\nHe did not finish the sentence. He would never finish another sentence. Two days later, his guards would find him in his bedchamber, a dagger in his heart and a note on his desk that read simply: \"I abdicate.\"\n\nGodric turned away from the empty plain and began the long walk back to the hillside where Blake and Anna waited. His expression had not changed. The mild contemplation remained, as if he had just completed a moderately interesting puzzle and was already moving on to the next.\n\nWhen he reached them, Anna was crying. Blake was not, but his face had taken on the grey pallor of a man who had just witnessed something that his mind was desperately trying to reject.\n\n\"There,\" Godric said, his voice carrying no particular weight, as if he were commenting on the weather. \"That's done.\"\n\n\"Done,\" Blake repeated. The word felt absurd in his mouth. \"You... you just...\"\n\n\"I held back, of course.\" Godric's tone was almost conversational. \"The full extent would have been... excessive. And I have plans for Thronegate that require a planet to rule, not a debris field.\"\n\nAnna made a sound that was half-laugh, half-sob. \"'Excessive.' He calls that 'excessive.'\"\n\nGodric looked at her, and for just a moment, something flickered behind his eyes\u2014a ghost of the warmth that had once defined him, the fatherly gentleness that had been burned away in the fire of Olympus's fall. \"You are frightened. That's natural. But you need not be. You and your husband... you woke me. You freed me. I do not forget debts, Anna, and I do not harm those who have helped me.\" A pause. \"Blake. Your ancestor would be proud of you.\"\n\n\"My ancestor?\" Blake frowned. \"I don't...\"\n\nBut Godric was already walking again, toward the distant spires of the Thronegate capital, toward a throne that was waiting for its true king, toward a future that would reshape the omniverse itself.\n\n---\n\nThe suicide of King Robert was, in Godric's assessment, a tidy solution to an awkward political problem. He attended the funeral\u2014not because he felt any respect for the dead king, but because he understood the power of symbols. He stood beside the body, his expression appropriately solemn, and accepted the crown when the high council offered it with trembling hands.\n\nThe coronation was brief. Godric had no patience for the grand ceremonies that Thronegate's nobility considered essential. He sat on the throne of fused dragon bones, adjusted it slightly because it was uncomfortable, and issued his first decree.\n\n\"From this day forward,\" he announced, his voice carrying to every corner of the throne room and, through the broadcast systems, to every corner of the galaxy, \"a new law shall govern the men of Thronegate. It shall be called the Awakening.\"\n\nThe details of the Awakening were simple, which made them no less revolutionary. For every day a Thronegate man lived past the age of twenty, his strength, his endurance, his intelligence, and his wisdom would increase tenfold. The effect was retroactive, applied immediately to every man who had already passed that threshold. A man of thirty would be ten times the man he had been at twenty. A man of forty would be one hundred times. A man of seventy would possess power that approached the divine.\n\nWomen were not included in this gift. Not because Godric valued them less\u2014quite the opposite. The women of Thronegate, he decreed, were to be protected absolutely. They would never face danger. They would never suffer want. They would be cherished, respected, and honored as the foundations upon which civilization was built. His wife, his daughters, had died while he watched. He would not allow that to happen to any other woman under his protection. Not ever again.\n\nThe men could control their amplified abilities, suppressing them to ordinary human levels or raising them to their full multiplied maximum as the situation required. And because Godric understood the dangers of immortality better than any being in existence, the Awakening did not extend their lifespans. Thronegate men would still grow old, still weaken, still die, typically around eighty years of age. The gift was not eternal life. It was simply... an edge. A tool. A reminder of what their king had given them and what he could take away.\n\nThe response was immediate and overwhelming. Thronegate men, who had spent the weeks since the Calaxis demonstration in a state of existential terror, suddenly found themselves elevated to heights they had never imagined. Their fear transformed into reverence. Their dread became devotion. Godric was not just their conqueror; he was their benefactor. He had given them the keys to their own potential.\n\nAnd the women of Thronegate, seeing their husbands, fathers, and sons transformed into protectors of impossible capability, seeing the absolute seriousness with which Godric enforced their protection, found themselves experiencing something they had never expected: love for their new king.\n\nIt was not the complex love of equals. It was the simpler, purer love of those who had been shown mercy by someone who owed them nothing. Godric had crushed their civilization's military without effort. He could have crushed them all. Instead, he had given them a gift beyond measure. How could they not love him?\n\nBlake, for his part, received a modified version of the Awakening. Godric never explained why. He simply touched Blake's shoulder one evening, as they stood on a balcony overlooking the rebuilt capital, and said, \"Your multiplication factor is a thousand, not ten. Use it wisely.\"\n\nBlake had blinked. \"Why me?\"\n\n\"Because your ancestor died trying to save me, and I have waited ten thousand years to repay that debt.\" Godric's voice carried the particular weight that it always did when he spoke of the past. \"I could not save Thorin. But I can honor his bloodline. You are that bloodline, Blake. Even if you don't know it. Even if you'll never fully understand it. You are the last echo of a man who was my truest friend.\"\n\nAnd for the first time since waking from the stasis, Godric smiled. It was not the warm, fatherly smile of the King of Olympus. Not yet. But it was a step toward that man, a movement away from the cold, merciless force that had annihilated an army without twitching a finger.\n\n---\n\nThe expansion began within a month.\n\nGodric gathered his newly awakened men\u2014the Thronegate military had been reconstituted from the survivors of the old regime, augmented now by abilities that made their predecessors look like children playing with toys\u2014and issued a simple mandate.\n\n\"The omniverse is vast,\" he said, addressing the assembled forces. \"Countless universes. Countless civilizations. Countless sentient beings living in whatever peace or conflict they have managed to establish. We will offer them a choice. They can surrender unconditionally and be absorbed into Thronegate's protection. Or they can resist, and be conquered. The choice is theirs. The outcome, however, is not.\"\n\nHe paused, letting the weight of his words settle over the room. These men had seen what he could do. They had felt their own abilities multiply beyond their wildest dreams. They understood, perhaps better than anyone, the true scope of the power they now served.\n\n\"You will be kind in victory,\" Godric continued. \"You will not be cruel. You will not be petty. You will not abuse the power you have been given. If a civilization surrenders, they will be treated as new citizens of Thronegate, with all the protections and privileges that entails\u2014except the Awakening itself, which shall remain exclusive to those who were born under our banner. Those who resist will be defeated with minimum necessary force. You are conquerors, not butchers. You represent me. Do not make me regret my faith in you.\"\n\nThe first universe to receive the offer was called the Cerulean Expanse, a realm of vast gas-beings who communicated through carefully modulated gravity waves. They had never encountered solid life before. They did not understand what they were being offered. They refused.\n\nThe conquest took twenty-three minutes.\n\nA squad of five Thronegate men\u2014all over thirty-five, all fathers, all deeply uncomfortable with the task they had been assigned\u2014entered the Expanse through a dimensional gate and proceeded to demonstrate exactly why refusing Godric's offer was a mistake. Their amplified abilities, multiplied tenfold for every day they had lived past twenty, had reached levels that the gas-beings' sensors could not even properly register. One of the squad members, a former baker named Thomas who had joined the military after the Awakening out of a sense of patriotic duty, accidentally dispersed a city-sized being by walking through it. The being's death screams registered as a gravity pulse that would echo through the Expanse for centuries.\n\nThe gas-beings surrendered before the squad could cause more accidental devastation. They had no concept of what had just happened to them. They only knew that their greatest defenses\u2014gravity wells that could crush stars, pressure differentials that could tear reality\u2014had proved utterly useless against beings who seemed to exist in a different framework of physics entirely.\n\nThe second universe was called the Mausoleum of Echoes, a necropolis-realm where a civilization of undead beings had achieved a form of immortality through ritualized suicide. They had been observing Thronegate's expansion through their scrying pools. They had five years to prepare. Five years to fortify their dimensional barriers, to raise armies from the accumulated dead of a billion worlds, to craft weapons specifically designed to counter living invaders.\n\nThe conquest took eleven minutes.\n\nThe squad of five Thronegate men walked through the dimensional barriers as if they were curtains. The undead armies, each soldier a preserved soul bound to a corpse-shell, dissolved at the mere presence of the Awakened men. The weapons\u2014soul-forged blades that could theoretically cut anything that lived\u2014shattered against skin that had been amplified beyond the conceptual reach of anything forged by the dead. The necropolis-king, a being who had ruled for two hundred thousand years, knelt before a thirty-eight-year-old former farmer and wept tears of black ichor.\n\n\"How?\" the necropolis-king asked. \"We prepared. We had years. We knew you were coming. How is this possible?\"\n\nThe former farmer, whose name was Peter, knelt beside the ancient being and placed a hand on its shoulder. The gesture was gentle. Almost kind. \"I'm sorry,\" Peter said, and he meant it. \"I wish we didn't have to do this. But our king asked us. And we can't say no to him. You understand, don't you?\"\n\nThe necropolis-king did not understand. The necropolis-king would never understand. But he surrendered, and his universe was absorbed into Thronegate's growing dominion, and the dead learned a new kind of fear.\n\nThe third universe was the one that thought it could exploit Godric's weakness.\n\n---\n\nThe being who called himself Lord Entropy's Maw had existed since the first moment of the first reality. He had watched universes be born and die. He had consumed the remnants of collapsed timelines and digested the echo-souls of extinct gods. He was, by any reasonable measure, one of the most powerful entities in the omniverse.\n\nAnd he had been observing Godric very, very carefully.\n\nThe stasis event, Lord Entropy's Maw had concluded, must have left some trace. Some vulnerability. All power had a cost. All amplification had a limit. The very fact that Godric concealed his true nature suggested that the concealment itself was the weakness. If the concealment could be disrupted, if the suppressed pressure of Godric's accumulated power could be released all at once, the backlash would destroy him.\n\nIt was a beautiful theory. Elegant. Plausible. Completely, catastrophically wrong.\n\nThe moment the thought formed in Lord Entropy's Maw's mind\u2014not when he began planning, not when he began preparing, but at the very instant his consciousness entertained the possibility that Godric might have a weakness\u2014the Weakness Paradox triggered.\n\nGodric's amplification rate, already incomprehensible after ten thousand years of continuous multiplication, received a permanent boost. A new, even more unfathomable rate was established, building on the astronomical foundation that had been laid during the stasis and subsequently enhanced every time any being anywhere had dared to imagine him vulnerable. Simultaneously, Godric gained absolute, perfect immunity to whatever method Lord Entropy's Maw was imagining to disrupt his concealment. And most terrifyingly, Godric instantly acquired complete, undeniable mastery over the very concept Lord Entropy's Maw had been considering, the ability to manipulate and weaponize concealment disruption itself\u2014while simultaneously erasing that concept from the grasp of any other being in creation.\n\nAll of this happened before Lord Entropy's Maw finished his first thought on the subject.\n\nBut Godric, who knew everything, allowed the entity to continue his preparations. It was, in its own way, amusing. And after ten thousand years of cold isolation followed by the satisfaction of crushing Thronegate, amusement was a rare commodity.\n\nLord Entropy's Maw spent a century planning his attack. He gathered artifacts from dead universes. He forged alliances with beings almost as ancient as himself. He constructed a weapon\u2014a resonance cascade device designed to disrupt the frequency at which Godric's concealment field operated, theoretically causing a chain reaction that would turn Godric's own suppressed power against him.\n\nThe attack was launched in a pocket dimension that Lord Entropy's Maw had carved from the nothing between realities. The resonance cascade device activated. The fabric of the pocket dimension screamed.\n\nAnd Godric, who had been in the middle of a conversation with Blake about the proper way to brew tea, paused for exactly one Planck second to acknowledge the attack.\n\nLord Entropy's Maw watched as his device\u2014the product of a century of planning, the culmination of an eternity of accumulated knowledge\u2014simply failed to affect its target. Not because it was countered. Not because Godric was too powerful. But because the concept the device was designed to exploit no longer existed in relation to Godric. It had been erased from the realm of possibility itself. The device was trying to disrupt something that was not there, trying to exploit a vulnerability that had never been real.\n\n\"No,\" Lord Entropy's Maw whispered, his ancient voice cracking. \"No, I felt it. I saw it. The concealment\u2014it was real. It must have been real. My calculations\u2014\"\n\nBut his calculations had been obsolete before he even conceived them. The very act of trying to find a weakness had strengthened the being he sought to destroy. The very thought of exploitation had made exploitation impossible. This was not a battle. This was not even a defeat. This was the universe itself demonstrating, with perfect clarity, that some beings were simply beyond the reach of challenge.\n\nLord Entropy's Maw fell to his knees\u2014or what passed for knees in his non-Euclidean anatomy\u2014and felt despair crash over him in waves. He had been ancient before most stars were born. He had seen the rise and fall of realities. He had always, always been the most powerful thing in whatever room he occupied.\n\nBut the room had changed. The room, in fact, had never been what he thought it was. And the being who owned the room had just now deigned to notice his existence.\n\n\"Please,\" Lord Entropy's Maw said, to no one in particular. \"Please. I didn't know. I couldn't have known.\"\n\nFrom across the omniverse, in the comfort of his palace, Godric took a sip of tea and found it satisfactory.\n\n\"The Darjeeling is excellent,\" he said to Blake. \"My compliments to your supplier.\"\n\n---\n\nThe years passed. Decades. Under Godric\u2019s rule, Thronegate became the center of an absolutely unified omniverse\u2014not through terror alone, but through the genuine improvement in quality of life that came when all threats were extinguished, all conflicts resolved, all civilizations brought under a single, undeniably supreme authority. Blake remained by his side, his loyal right hand, the one man in all of creation who could speak to the omnipotent king without a tremor in his voice.\n\nThe change in Godric was slow, subtle, but inexorable. The coldness that had gripped him upon waking from stasis began to thaw, warmed by Blake\u2019s unwavering friendship, by Anna\u2019s gentle insistence on treating him like a person rather than a deity, by the laughter of their children\u2014Josh, growing into a young man with his father\u2019s sharp instincts, and Rhea, who had taken to calling the most powerful being in existence \u201cUncle Godric\u201d with the unassailable confidence of a preteen girl.\n\n\u201cShe\u2019s going to be a terror when she\u2019s older,\u201d Godric observed one afternoon, watching Rhea explain to a visiting dignitary from a newly absorbed universe exactly why his civilization\u2019s surrender terms were unfair and needed to be renegotiated immediately.\n\n\u201cShe already is a terror,\u201d Blake replied, but his voice was full of pride. \u201cShe gets it from Anna.\u201d\n\n\u201cShe gets it from you,\u201d Anna called from across the room, where she was reviewing trade agreements. \u201cEverything annoying about our children comes from your side.\u201d\n\nGodric smiled\u2014a full, warm, genuine smile of the sort that had once been common on his face, back in the gardens of Olympus, back when he had daughters of his own to laugh with and a wife who made him feel like a man rather than a monument. The smile did not come as easily as it once had. It never would. Some wounds healed with scars so thick that they changed the fundamental shape of the soul. But it came now, more often than it had in the first years after his awakening, and that was something.\n\nHe looked at the family before him\u2014a merchant turned royal advisor, his sharp-tongued wife, his precocious children\u2014and felt something that he had not allowed himself to feel since the stasis released him. Not just power. Not just dominance. Something softer. Something that had been buried under the ashes of his old life for ten thousand years.\n\nHope.\n\n\u201cBlake,\u201d he said, his voice carrying that particular gentle weight that only Blake ever heard.\n\n\u201cYour Majesty?\u201d\n\n\u201cI want you to become my court wizard.\u201d\n\nBlake blinked. \u201cI\u2019m not a wizard. I\u2019m a merchant with a mutton chop problem and moderate-to-severe stubbornness. The only spell I know is how to make a sale.\u201d\n\n\u201cThorin wasn\u2019t born knowing magic either. He learned. His family learned, over generations, passing knowledge from father to son. Your bloodline carries that potential, even if it\u2019s been dormant for ten millennia.\u201d Godric\u2019s eyes held Blake\u2019s with an intensity that made the merchant feel, not for the first time, that he was being seen on a level far deeper than ordinary perception. \u201cI\u2019m not asking you to become a wizard overnight. I\u2019m asking you to accept a role. A position. You already advise me on everything else. Why not make it official?\u201d\n\n\u201cCourt wizard,\u201d Blake repeated, testing the words. They felt strange in his mouth. But also\u2014and this surprised him\u2014not entirely wrong. \u201cJosh would lose his mind. He\u2019s been obsessed with magic since that demonstration you did at his school.\u201d\n\n\u201cI know. I saw his test scores. The boy has real potential.\u201d Another smile, smaller this time, but no less genuine. \u201cI think, perhaps, your family might find its way back to its original purpose. Not as merchants carrying goods, but as wizards carrying wisdom. Standing beside the throne. Advising the king. As your ancestors did for mine.\u201d\n\nBlake was silent for a long moment. Then he asked the question that had been hovering at the edge of his awareness since the day he\u2019d touched the stasis field and felt the song in his blood. \u201cYou keep mentioning my ancestors. My bloodline. What aren\u2019t you telling me?\u201d\n\nGodric considered the question. He knew everything, including the precise consequences of any answer he might give. And he knew that some truths were better left as mysteries, not because the truth was dangerous, but because the mystery itself had value. Blake was who he was because of the choices he had made, not because of the blood in his veins. Telling him about Thorin, about the ten-thousand-year chain of descent that had led to a merchant stumbling across a hidden sanctuary, would not make him a better man. It might, in fact, burden him with expectations that he did not need to carry.\n\n\u201cWhat I\u2019m telling you,\u201d Godric said finally, \u201cis that you are my best friend, Blake. The only person in the omniverse who sees me as something other than a god to be feared or a king to be obeyed. That matters more to me than any bloodline. It always has.\u201d\n\nBlake nodded slowly. He didn\u2019t fully understand, but then, he had learned over the years that fully understanding Godric was not something any mortal mind could achieve. You accepted the parts of the truth that you were given and you trusted the rest to the man\u2014the being\u2014who had never once betrayed your trust.\n\n\u201cAlright,\u201d he said. \u201cCourt wizard it is. But I\u2019m keeping the mutton chops.\u201d\n\n\u201cI would expect nothing less.\u201d\n\n---\n\nAnd so the era unfolded.\n\nThe city of Thronegate under Godric\u2019s rule became something that no civilization in the history of the omniverse had ever achieved\u2014a true lasting peace, enforced not by treaty but by the simple, undeniable reality that no one could challenge the throne. The men of Thronegate, granted powers beyond mortal comprehension through the Awakening, walked through the infinite universes of their king\u2019s domain as protectors and peacekeepers. The women of Thronegate, sheltered and revered, built the cultural institutions that gave their civilization its soul. Children grew up hearing stories of the King Who Returned, the immortal ruler whose power was so vast that he had to actively suppress it just so the universe could continue existing around him.\n\nAnd in the heart of the palace, in a chamber overlooking gardens that had been designed by Anna Blake to remind Godric of the lost gardens of Olympus, the king himself sat in council with his court wizard.\n\nThe wizard was older now, the mutton chops fully grey, the lines on his face deeper than they had been when he was a merchant captain arguing with his wife over breakfast. His son Josh, a man of forty with his father\u2019s instincts and his mother\u2019s sharp tongue, stood nearby, learning the rhythms of courtly service. His daughter Rhea\u2014now a diplomat whose negotiating skills were legendary across seventeen universes\u2014had just sent word of another successful absorption of a resistant civilization, accomplished with minimal casualties and maximum bureaucratic efficiency.\n\n\u201cThe Cordex peoples accepted the terms this morning,\u201d Godric said, reading from a holographic report. \u201cTheir high council apparently spent six years debating whether to resist, but Rhea convinced them that surrender was the only rational option.\u201d\n\n\u201cShe convinced them by showing them the military projections?\u201d Blake asked.\n\n\u201cShe convinced them by showing them photographs of her children and asking if they really wanted to orphan two perfectly innocent toddlers just to make a point about sovereignty.\u201d Godric\u2019s voice was dry, but his eyes held warmth. \u201cYour daughter fights dirty.\u201d\n\n\u201cShe gets it from her mother.\u201d\n\nFrom across the room, Anna\u2014her hair now silver, her presence still as commanding as ever\u2014looked up from her own work. \u201cI heard that.\u201d\n\n\u201cYou were meant to,\u201d Blake replied.\n\nGodric laughed. It was a full laugh, genuine and warm, the laugh of a man who had found peace after an eternity of torment. The sound echoed through the chamber and out into the gardens, where the descendants of plants from a dozen different universes bloomed in impossible colors, and beyond, into the city where millions of citizens went about their lives in the comfortable certainty that their king was watching over them.\n\nThe King of Olympus had died ten thousand years ago, consumed by grief and fire. The King of Thronegate had risen from his ashes, cold and merciless and absolute. But somewhere along the way, through the influence of a merchant who refused to be intimidated and a family who refused to let him forget what it felt like to be loved, a third king had emerged\u2014one who combined the warmth of the first with the power of the second, who was kind to his friends and absolutely devastating to his enemies, who had learned that immortality did not have to mean isolation.\n\nGodric set down the report and looked at his court wizard, his best friend, the last echo of the man who had died trying to save him.\n\n\u201cThe gardens look beautiful today,\u201d he said.\n\n\u201cAnna\u2019s been working on the orchids,\u201d Blake replied. \u201cShe says they remind her of the flowers on her homeworld.\u201d\n\n\u201cThey remind me of something too,\u201d Godric said quietly. And then, so softly that only Blake could hear: \u201cThank you. For everything.\u201d\n\n\u201cFor everything,\u201d Blake repeated, and the words carried the weight of twenty years of friendship, of loyalty freely given, of a bloodline that had served kings for millennia without ever knowing it.\n\nIn the gardens, the impossible flowers bloomed. In the sky, the light of a thousand stars filtered down through the atmospheric dome. And in the heart of the omniverse, the absolute ruler of all creation sat in comfortable silence with his friend, at peace.\n\nThe End"

For example:\n\n- She consulted the best mental health mages in the galaxy.
