When activated, the machine simply deconstructed itself, its parts scattering as if trying to escape.\n- She traveled to the far edges of the omniverse, to a planet where Godric's influence was said to be thinner. The journey was treacherous. When she arrived, the inhabitants had apparently received a divine revelation that they must not interfere with \"the king's touch.\" They imprisoned her for a day and deported her.\n- In desperation, she tried to create a counter-memory: using a reality sculptor (a rare artifact) to overwrite the memory with something pleasant. The artifact, when applied, sparked and emitted a sound like a scream, then melted into inert metal.\n\nEach failure made Rogr worse because it reminded him of the event. She began to suspect that the universe itself was preventing a cure because it would be a slight against Godric's power. She never voiced this, but it terrified her.\n\n**Part 5: Blake's Visit**\n\nA knock on the door. Rosa opens to find a man with a sheepish, guilt-ridden expression. He asks for Rogr and her. She recognizes him: Blake, the merchant turned court wizard, the king's best friend. Her heart races. She invites him in, nervous.\n\nBlake's confession: he and Godric often joked around. One day, Blake teased Godric that his subjects from new universes expected him to be a tyrant because of the conquest stories. He said, \"Why not give them a show? Pretend to be furious, just for a second.\" Godric, who loves a good prank, agreed. When the delegation arrived, he borrowed a tiny fraction of his presence and directed a fleeting thought of \"mild displeasure\" at them. It was supposed to be for fun, to see them jump. Godric held back 99.999...% of his power. He thought it would be a small scare. He did not realize that even that infinitesimal sliver would shatter mortal minds.\n\nBlake says he only learned about Rogr's condition a few days ago, when Godric mentioned it in passing: \"I still wonder why that one diplomat never recovered. Mortals can be so delicate.\" Blake was horrified. He shouted at Godric, \"You broke a man and didn't even bother to check on him?\" Godric, taken aback, replied that he thought Rogr would \"tough it out.\" He'd been mortal once, he believed in resilience. Blake demanded to fix it, and Godric agreed.\n\nNow Blake is here, asking permission to bring Godric's healing.\n\n**Part 6: Deliberation**\n\nRosa's thoughts explode. Anger at Blake, anger at Godric, but also love for Godric. She feels guilty for being angry. She looks at Rogr, who has been listening from his corner. Rogr\u2019s eyes are wide with fear. He whispers, \"No, he'll be displeased again. I can't.\" Rosa takes his hand, tells him they have to try. Pete, their son, now a young man, is torn. He says, \"But the king is good... he wouldn't hurt us on purpose. We should trust him.\" After a long, painful discussion, Rosa makes the decision. She nods to Blake. \"Please, help him.\"\n\n**Part 7: The Cure**\n\nThe moment she says yes, Godric is simply there. No transition. The atmosphere becomes heavy, not oppressive but dense, as if reality holds its breath. Rosa can't move, can't think clearly. She sees Godric's face: calm, perhaps a hint of sadness and kindness. He glances at Rogr. Rogr gasps, sits up straight, the pallor washes away, his eyes become clear. He looks around, confused but vibrant. He sees Rosa and smiles\u2014the first real smile in a decade. Rosa rushes to embrace him, sobbing.\n\nGodric speaks: \"It's done. I apologize for the delay.\" His voice is deep and gentle. It makes her want to kneel. He offers compensation, an absurd list: a palace, an entire system, the ability to grant her own wishes. She refuses, her voice shaking. She can't accept anything; it would feel like payment for suffering she can't quantify. He nods, says it's her choice, and offers his respect. Then he is gone.\n\n**Part 8: Emotional Aftermath**\n\nThe family sits in stunned silence. Rogr is marveling at how good he feels, even his old knee injury is gone. Pete is babbling about having met the king. Rosa feels a storm: overwhelming joy, relief, gratitude that brings tears, but underneath, a cold, creeping dread. It was so easy. A decade of her life, ruined therapies, shattered hope\u2014solved in an instant. Not even an instant. Less than a heartbeat. And not just cured, but enhanced. She realizes that every moment of her struggle was meaningless in the face of his power. She tries to push the dread away, to focus on Rogr, but it lingers.\n\n**Part 9: Lingering Discord**\n\nDays later, life has improved. Rogr is back to work, better than ever. Pete won't stop talking about the king. Everywhere she goes, she hears praise for Godric: his justice, his kindness. She joins in because it's true. But at night, she lies awake, remembering the presence, the unbearable weight of his existence pressing on her mind. She can't explain it to anyone. She loves Godric. She truly does. But she also fears him in a way that has no words.\n\n**Part 10: The Joke**\n\nMaybe a week later, Rosa is invited to the palace to receive official thanks or something? Or perhaps Blake visits again to check on them. He seems relieved. They chat. Then, in the corridor, she overhears Godric's voice, light and amused: \"You know, Blake, I've been thinking. The delegates from the Vortex Sector are due next month. They're a bit too smug for my liking. What do you say we give them a taste of the tyrant? Just a tiny one. A little jolt.\" Blake's response is a choked noise, half-laugh, half-despair. \"Your Majesty, please. No more pranks.\" Rosa freezes, her blood going cold. The story ends on that chilling note.\n\nNow we need to write it in Rosa's first-person, present tense or past? The instructions don't specify tense, but typically, 1st person can be past or present. For horror, present tense can be more immediate. But past tense is easier for flashbacks. I'll use past tense for reflection and present for some scenes. Better to stick with past tense for consistency, as she narrates the events that have happened.\n\nWe need to weave all this into a continuous narrative, avoiding sections that seem like separate parts. Use prose, descriptive, sensory.\n\nLet's begin writing the actual text.\n\n---\n\nI'll draft now in full. Word count target: 3000-3500, so we have to be detailed but not rambling.\n\n**Start:**\n\nThe bedroom smelled of old fear. That was a thing I\u2019d learned over the past decade\u2014fear had a scent, a greasy kind of musk that seeped into sheets and pillows and would not wash out no matter how many times I boiled the fabric. It clung to the walls, to the dark curtains I kept drawn because sunlight made Rogr scream. It clung to me, probably, though I\u2019d stopped noticing my own smell long ago.\n\nI sat on the edge of the bed, my hand resting on Rogr\u2019s shoulder. He was curled so tight, his knees drawn up to his chest, his arms wrapped around his head. Not sleeping\u2014he never truly slept anymore, only dropped into these trembling trances where his eyes moved rapidly behind his lids and his lips formed words I could not hear. A decade of this. Ten years of watching my husband shrink from a vibrant, curious linguist into a creature that flinched at shadows and wept at the slightest loud noise.\n\n\u201cRogr,\u201d I whispered, not because I expected an answer but because the silence sometimes felt like it would swallow us both. \u201cI\u2019m here. I love you.\u201d\n\nHis breathing hitched. That was the only acknowledgment I ever got.\n\nOutside our modest home, Thronegate basked in its golden age. I could hear distant laughter from the market square, the rumble of transports carrying goods from a hundred universes. The Awakening had made our men into something godlike, and the king\u2019s protection made us women safe beyond our ancestors\u2019 wildest dreams. My son Pete, fifteen now, spent his evenings at the training grounds, learning to control the power that had blossomed in him on his twentieth birthday\u2014less than a year away. He idolized King Godric. Everyone did.\n\nI did.\n\nAnd that was the part that made my head feel like it was splitting in two whenever I thought about it for too long. I loved the king. I was grateful for his rule, for the peace, for the absolute certainty that no outside force could ever threaten my family. When I saw his face on the public holos\u2014that strong, bearded jaw, those kind eyes, the salt-and-pepper hair that framed a face both fatherly and commanding\u2014my heart swelled with a reverence I cannot describe. He was more than a ruler. He was the axis around which the omniverse turned.\n\nBut he was also the reason my husband had not spoken a complete sentence in a decade.\n\nI didn\u2019t understand it. That was the worst part. The event\u2014the infamous \u201cbad day\u201d as I called it in my own head\u2014had been so small. A diplomatic delegation, a routine introduction. Rogr had been a junior aide, thrilled to be chosen. He\u2019d left that morning bouncing on his heels, and he\u2019d come back that afternoon as a hollowed-out shell. Over the years, I\u2019d pieced together fragments of what happened: the king had been\u2026 displeased. Not at Rogr specifically, but at the group. A flash of something cold in his eyes. A weight in the air that Rogr described as \u201call the gravity in the universe pressing on my soul.\u201d It lasted less than a second. The king\u2019s expression had returned to its usual warmth immediately, and the rest of the meeting had proceeded normally.\n\nBut that fraction of a heartbeat had been enough. Rogr\u2019s mind had cracked like an eggshell.\n\n---\n\nI tried everything. Gods, I tried everything.\n\nAt first, I took him to the best physicians Thronegate had to offer. They ran their scanners, poked at his neural pathways, and then one by one they would grow pale. Not because they found a tumor or a chemical imbalance\u2014they couldn\u2019t find anything. But they felt something. One doctor, a middle-aged woman whose reputation stretched across three galaxies, started trembling as she examined him. She backed away, her instruments clattering to the floor, and fled the room without a word. She quit practicing the next day. I still do not know what she sensed.\n\nThen I turned to the magicians. The Awakening had amplified Thronegate\u2019s arcane talents as well, and there were spell-weavers who could supposedly reknit a damaged psyche. The first one I hired, a kindly old man named Halvor, sat with Rogr for three hours, chanting softly. At the end, he came out of the room weeping. \u201cI can\u2019t,\u201d he said. \u201cThe memory\u2014it\u2019s not just a memory. It\u2019s like\u2026 it\u2019s like the universe itself agrees with the king\u2019s momentary displeasure. To erase it would be to challenge the architect of reality. I can\u2019t. I\u2019m sorry.\u201d I didn\u2019t understand his words then. I do now.\n\nI spent our life savings on a device called the Mnemonic Purifier, smuggled from a universe so distant that its physics were almost incompatible with our own. It was supposed to extract traumatic memory patterns and neutralize them. When I activated it, the machine let out a sound I can only describe as a high-pitched whimper, and then its components disassembled themselves with such speed and precision that in three seconds there was nothing but a pile of individual atoms on the floor, arranged in a perfect geometric pattern. It had destroyed itself rather than touch Rogr\u2019s mind.\n\nI grew desperate. I heard rumors of a pocket dimension\u2014a fold in space where Godric\u2019s influence was supposedly thinner, where his omniscience might be strained. The journey took me three standard months. When I arrived, the inhabitants, a species of gaseous philosophers, detained me at their border and explained through a translator that they had received a divine edict: \u201cDo not interfere with the king\u2019s touch.\u201d They were terribly apologetic, but they said they could not risk his displeasure, even if that displeasure was aimed elsewhere. I screamed at them until I lost my voice. They deported me gently but firmly.\n\nEach failure made Rogr worse. He would see me trying, see the hope in my eyes, and then see it die, and something in him would flinch away further. He stopped eating properly. He stopped speaking entirely. My son watched his father decay and watched his mother fail, and he compensated by doubling down on his worship of the king. Pete would sit beside me at night and say, \u201cMother, the king is good. He\u2019s the best thing that ever happened to us. Whatever happened to Father, it must have been a mistake. The king doesn\u2019t make mistakes, so maybe Father\u2026 maybe Father just wasn\u2019t strong enough.\u201d I wanted to slap him. I wanted to hug him. I said nothing.\n\n---\n\nIt was a cool autumn evening when Blake came to our door. I knew his face instantly\u2014the mutton chops, the weathered merchant\u2019s hands, the eyes that carried a weight that might have been wisdom or might have been guilt. The king\u2019s best friend. The court wizard. I had seen him on holos a thousand times, always standing just behind Godric\u2019s shoulder, the only person in the omniverse who could crack a joke in the throne room without everyone freezing in terror.\n\n\u201cMrs. Rosa?\u201d he asked, his voice surprisingly gentle. \u201cI think we need to talk.\u201d\n\nI let him in because what else could I do? He sat in our small living room, his hands clasped between his knees, and he told me everything. The prank. The offhand comment he\u2019d made to Godric years ago: \u201cYou know, Your Majesty, the new delegates all expect a tyrant because of the conquest stories. Why not give them a little scare just for fun?\u201d Godric, who trusted Blake completely, had taken the idea and run with it. He\u2019d decided to borrow a minuscule fraction of his presence\u2014a sliver so small that to him it felt like a playful wink\u2014and direct a fleeting thought of \u201cmild displeasure\u201d at the delegation. Just for a second. Just to see them squirm. He\u2019d suppressed 99.999\u2026 percent of his power, a percentage with so many nines after the decimal that my mortal mind couldn\u2019t hold it. He honestly believed it would be harmless.\n\n\u201cHe\u2019s not cruel, you have to understand,\u201d Blake said, his voice cracking. \u201cHe spent ten thousand years as a frozen weapon. He\u2019s forgotten what it\u2019s like to be breakable. When I told him about Rogr\u2014when he casually mentioned that \u2018one diplomat never recovered, pity\u2019\u2014I\u2026 I shouted at him. I yelled at the most powerful being in existence. And he just blinked at me and said, \u2018Rosa\u2019s husband? But I barely touched him. I thought the man would bounce back. Mortals are stronger than they look.\u2019\u201d Blake\u2019s fists clenched. \u201cThat\u2019s when I realized he genuinely had no idea. He wasn\u2019t being malicious. He just\u2026 miscalculated. By a scale that would take a thousand mathematicians to quantify.\u201d\n\nI sat there, my body numb, my mind reeling. The source of my husband\u2019s decade of hell was a joke. A prank. A momentary lark between two old friends. The king held back almost everything, and it still shattered a man. And I\u2014I had spent years crawling through the omniverse trying to undo a damage that was, by its very nature, an edict from the throne of creation, however unintentional.\n\nI wanted to hate Blake. I wanted to hate Godric. But the same heart that loved my husband also loved my king, and the king had been genuinely kind to everyone I\u2019d ever known. The merchants who\u2019d been cheated before the conquest now traded fairly. The planets that had starved now had food. My son was going to live in a world without war. How do you hate that? How do you reconcile that?\n\n\u201cI\u2019m here,\u201d Blake said, his voice barely above a whisper, \u201cto ask your permission. Let me bring Godric here to fix this. He will. I\u2019ve made sure of it. He\u2019ll do it in an instant, no fuss. But it has to be your choice.\u201d\n\nI looked over at the darkened bedroom where Rogr lay. Pete was standing in the doorway now, having come home silently. His eyes were wide. He had heard everything. He loved the king more than anyone. And he was hearing that the king had broken his father by accident, for fun. I could see the conflict tearing at his young face.\n\n\u201cRogr?\u201d I called softly. I went to him, knelt by the bed. \u201cRogr, please. I know you\u2019re in there. The king\u2019s friend is here. He wants to help. The king himself will help. Do you want that?\u201d\n\nRogr\u2019s trembling intensified. For the first time in months, his eyes opened fully. There was terror there, but there was also a desperate, trapped awareness. He tried to speak. His lips formed words, but only a croak came out. I leaned close and caught the barest whisper: \u201cPlease\u2026 make it stop.\u201d\n\nPete stepped forward, his voice trembling. \u201cMother, let them. Please. If the king is as good as we\u2019ve always believed, he\u2019ll fix it.\u201d\n\nI looked at Blake. \u201cYes,\u201d I said. \u201cDo it.\u201d\n\n---\n\nThe moment the word left my mouth, the air in the room changed. It didn\u2019t move\u2014it thickened, became dense as honey, became heavy as the heart of a star. My lungs labored to draw breath. My thoughts slowed, each one crawling through my mind as if wading through syrup. And then Godric was there.\n\nI never saw him arrive. He was simply standing by the foot of the bed, as if he had always been there, as if the universe had rearranged itself around his presence in a fraction of a fraction of a moment and my senses were too slow to register the change. He was exactly as he appeared on the holos: the powerful build, the close-cropped hair with its distinguished silvering, the neatly trimmed salt-and-pepper beard, the face that could be a warm father or a merciless king depending on the tilt of his brow. He wore a simple tunic, nothing regal, but his sheer existence turned the modest bedroom into a cathedral.\n\nI could not move. My daughter-in-law\u2019s instinct\u2014or a supplicant\u2019s instinct\u2014told me to kneel, to avert my eyes, to do something to show respect. My muscles would not obey. Not because I was paralyzed, but because my body recognized, on a level far deeper than conscious thought, that I was in the presence of a power that could unmake me with a stray thought. Fighting the instinct to kneel was like fighting the instinct to breathe; it was simply not an option. So I knelt. Pete knelt beside me. Blake remained standing, his face a mask of complex emotion.\n\nGodric looked at Rogr. That was all. Just a look. No gesture, no word, no flash of light. His eyes\u2014grey, I think, or maybe a color that doesn\u2019t exist in mortal vision\u2014settled on my husband\u2019s trembling form, and in the space between one heartbeat and the next, Rogr stopped trembling.\n\nIt was that fast. A decade of agony, a decade of watching my husband disintegrate, a decade of failed therapies and shattered artifacts and journeys to the edges of reality\u2014all of it resolved in less than a single heartbeat. Rogr\u2019s body uncurled. The pallid grey of his skin flushed with healthy color. The deep lines of trauma around his eyes and mouth smoothed away. His breathing steadied into a deep, peaceful rhythm. He blinked, and I saw his eyes focus\u2014truly focus\u2014for the first time in years.\n\n\u201cRosa?\u201d he said. His voice was hoarse from disuse, but it was his voice. The voice of the man I\u2019d married. \u201cWhat\u2026 what happened? I feel\u2026\u201d\n\nHe sat up, and I saw him notice his own body with wonder. He flexed his fingers, turned his hands over, touched his own face. The small physical ailments that had plagued him even before the trauma\u2014the stiff knee from an old sports injury, the chronic ache in his shoulder\u2014were gone. His skin looked like it did in his youth, not de-aged, but robust, vibrant, perfect in a way that had nothing to do with age and everything to do with health. He was the very picture of vitality, a man who had never suffered a day in his life.\n\nMy mind stumbled over the impossibility. All my efforts, all the money I\u2019d spent, all the hopes I\u2019d lost\u2014they had been less than a whisper against a hurricane. The king had not moved a single muscle. He had not drawn upon any visible power. I didn\u2019t even know if he had intentionally done it, or if the healing had simply happened as a side effect of his attention, the way a candle flame incidentally warms the air around it.\n\nI rushed to Rogr, threw my arms around him, and wept. I felt his arms come up to hold me, strong and certain. I heard Pete let out a choked laugh, then rush forward to join us. For a long, suspended moment, we were just a family again, whole again.\n\nAnd then Godric spoke, and the universe snapped back into focus.\n\n\u201cI\u2019m told this was my fault,\u201d he said, his voice a low, resonant baritone that seemed to come from everywhere at once. \u201cI\u2019m told I miscalculated. It\u2019s a\u2026 difficult concept to adjust to. I held back almost all of my power\u2014truly, I did. I didn\u2019t wish to cause harm. But I\u2019m beginning to understand that even \u2018almost all\u2019 is a relative figure.\u201d He paused, and there was something almost like regret in his tone. \u201cI\u2019m sorry, Rogr. Rosa. It was never my intention to cause lasting pain.\u201d\n\nAn apology. From the king of the omniverse. My heart swelled with something that was half love and half overwhelming, suffocating dread. He was sorry. He meant it. He was good.\n\nBut the ease of it. The terrifying, inconceivable ease.\n\nGodric\u2019s attention shifted to me. Even though his expression was gentle, I felt the weight of that gaze like a physical thing. I understood then why Rogr had broken. The king\u2019s mild displeasure must have been a thousand times heavier than this, and this was already nearly too much for my mind to bear.\n\n\u201cI am aware of the burden you\u2019ve carried, Rosa,\u201d he said. \u201cThe doctors. The journeys. The hope you poured into a universe that, I must admit, was probably too afraid of me to help you. I would like to offer compensation. Not as payment\u2014nothing can pay for ten years of your life\u2014but as a gesture. Whatever you desire. Wealth. A palace. A position for your son in the highest echelons of my court. If you wish it, I can give you a world of your own, a place where you and your family can live in whatever manner you choose, free of any obligation. I can grant you abilities beyond the Awakening. I can\u2014\u201d\n\nI held up my hand, and the act of interrupting the most powerful being in existence was so audacious that I almost fainted on the spot. But I had spent a decade fighting impossible odds. Somewhere in me, there was a core of stubbornness that even Godric\u2019s presence couldn\u2019t melt.\n\n\u201cNo,\u201d I whispered. \u201cNo, thank you, my king.\u201d\n\nHe stopped. Looked at me with something that might have been curiosity, might have been respect.\n\n\u201cI just wanted my husband back,\u201d I continued, my voice shaking. \u201cI wanted my family. I wanted him to be okay. You gave me that. The rest\u2026 it would feel wrong. Like I was being paid for my suffering, and that\u2019s not\u2014that\u2019s not what I want to take from you. Please, just\u2026 let us go back to normal. That\u2019s all the compensation I need.\u201d\n\nFor a long moment, Godric was silent. Then he nodded\u2014a singular, deliberate motion\u2014and his expression shifted into something that was unmistakably warm. Not the terrifying warmth of a god humoring a mortal, but a genuine, human warmth, the kind I imagined he\u2019d shown to his own daughters long ago.\n\n\u201cYou\u2019re very brave, Rosa,\u201d he said. \u201cOr very stubborn. Or both. I hope you know that the offer remains, should you ever change your mind. For now, though, you will have your normal life. I promise.\u201d\n\nAnd then, without any transition, he was gone. The air lightened. My lungs remembered how to work. My thoughts sped back up. The room was just a room again.\n\nRogr was holding me. Pete was crying. Blake was standing in the corner, his expression a mixture of relief and a guilt I knew he\u2019d carry for the rest of his life.\n\n---\n\nThe days that followed were strange.\n\nRogr\u2019s recovery was so complete that it bordered on the miraculous\u2014no, that was the wrong word. Miracles implied divine intervention that left a trace of awe. This was simply a fact: my husband was well. Not just recovered, but better than he had ever been. His mind was sharp, his body robust. He went back to work within a week, and within two he was promoted. He talked about the king with the same reverence everyone else did, perhaps even more. He had felt the king\u2019s attention twice now: once as the careless brunt of a joke, and once as the deliberate focus of healing. He somehow loved Godric for both.\n\nPete was overjoyed. He\u2019d been given a brief glimpse of the king in person, and to him that was the greatest honor of his life. He didn\u2019t talk about the bad parts. He simply couldn\u2019t hold the contradiction in his mind, or wouldn\u2019t.\n\nAnd me? I loved Godric. I truly did. Every morning I woke up and saw my husband\u2019s peaceful face and I was flooded with gratitude so intense it brought me to tears. The king had fixed him. The king had apologized. The king was good.\n\nBut every night, when the darkness came, I lay awake and felt the weight again. Not the weight of his presence\u2014that had been dispelled. But the weight of understanding. The memory of that fraction of a second when the universe itself bent to his will and my decade of suffering was erased as an afterthought. I could not shake the image of that disassembling machine, the atoms arranging themselves in perfect geometry to avoid offending him. I could not forget the gas-beings who had received a divine edict not to interfere with \u201cthe king\u2019s touch,\u201d as if his casual whims were writ into the fabric of creation.\n\nHe was good. He was kind. He was just. And he was so far beyond us that the entire omniverse was a fragile bubble held together by his restraint. That was the horror. Not cruelty. Not malice. Just\u2026 scale.\n\nI never spoke of this to anyone. Who would understand? To them, he was the perfect king. To me, he was the perfect king. But I had been given a glimpse behind the curtain, and that glimpse had carved something into me that I do not think will ever heal.\n\n---\n\nTwo weeks after Godric\u2019s visit, Blake stopped by to check on us. He looked older than I remembered, the guilt still visible around his eyes. He sat with us in the living room, and we talked about small things\u2014weather, trade routes, the upcoming festival. Pete pestered him with questions about his travels. Rogr laughed, a sound I would never tire of.\n\nAt some point, I went to the kitchen to prepare tea. The window was open, and from outside I heard voices drifting up from the garden path. Blake\u2019s voice, recognizable, and another\u2014the deeper, resonant tone that made my skin prickle even now.\n\nI froze, instinctively eavesdropping.\n\n\u201c\u2026so I\u2019ve been thinking,\u201d Godric was saying, his tone light, conversational. \u201cThe delegation from the Vortex Sector is due next month. You remember them. The ones who think their dimensional-twisting swords make them special. What do you say we give them a little tyrant, just for a moment? I could be very convincing. I\u2019d hold back, of course. Even more than last time. I\u2019m learning, you see.\u201d\n\nBlake\u2019s reply was a strangled noise\u2014half laugh, half despair. \u201cYour Majesty, please. No. No more pranks. The last one took ten years off my life span, and I wasn\u2019t even the one traumatized. Let\u2019s just\u2026 let\u2019s just serve tea and be nice.\u201d\n\nA chuckle, warm and deep. \u201cYou\u2019re no fun, Blake. Fine. Tea and nice it is. But someday, I\u2019m going to find the perfect joke\u2014one that\u2019s funny for everyone involved.\u201d\n\n\u201cYour Majesty, with respect, you have the humor detection of a black hole.\u201d\n\n\u201cA black hole that could unmake you, though.\u201d\n\n\u201cThat\u2019s my point.\u201d\n\nAnd then they both laughed, the easy laughter of old friends.\n\nI stood in the kitchen, my hand clutching the tea kettle, and I felt the dread settle back into my bones. Not because I thought Godric would ever hurt us again. He wouldn\u2019t. He\u2019d learned, he was careful, he was good. But the casualness of it. The \u201csomeday.\u201d The fact that the most powerful being in existence saw trauma as a matter of calibration\u2014a little more restraint here, a little less there\u2014as if mortal minds were instruments he was learning to tune.\n\nI loved him. I feared him. I was grateful to him. I wished I had never met him.\n\nAll of these things were true at once, and the weight of holding them together was a different kind of trauma.\n\nI carried the tea out to my family, and I smiled, and I sat beside my healthy husband, and I did not say a word about what I\u2019d heard.\n\nWhat could I say?\n\nI lived in a perfect kingdom under a perfect king. I was happy. I was terrified. And I would be both for the rest of my life.\n\nThe end.\n\n---\n\nWe need to ensure it's 3000-3500 words. The above is roughly there; we can expand. Let's refine and flesh out some sections, especially the \"absurdly elaborate attempts.\" We can add more sensory details, internal monologue, and perhaps another failed attempt or two to heighten the despair. But he didn't interfere because he genuinely thought it wasn't that bad. That is crucial.\n\nWe should also show Rogr's personality before, to contrast. And Rosa's love for him. Make the reader feel the loss.\n\nI'll incorporate more details about the trauma: Rogr's inability to even name what he experienced. \"It wasn't his face. It was just... a feeling. Like the universe was angry at me. Like I had done something so wrong that the very stars wanted me dead.\" And he can't explain it.\n\nAnd the attempts: maybe Rosa tried to get Thronegate authorities involved, but they couldn't do anything because it was the king's doing. The bureaucracy itself would freeze.\n\nI'll add a section where Rosa, in absolute desperation, tried to confront the king directly, but she couldn't even get an audience because she's a commoner, and her requests were lost in the system. Or she managed to get a hearing, but Godric wasn't there, and the officials dismissed her. This might be before Blake came.\n\nBut the prompt says she must not involve Godric or Blake in her attempts, so she might have tried to involve lower-level officials, but it failed due to fear.\n\nLet's expand.\n\nAlso, after Godric cures Rogr, we need to highlight the \"prolonged existential dread\" in Rosa. Perhaps she becomes hyper-aware of small things: a cup not breaking when it falls, a coincidence, and she wonders if Godric's attention is on them again. It's paranoia mixed with reverence.\n\nWe can end with the joke scene, which I've already included, but maybe make it more direct: maybe Rosa and Rogr are invited to the palace for a small reception, and she wanders into the garden and overhears them. That would be natural.\n\nI'll adjust: Blake visits, and during the visit, Godric appears again (maybe he just pops in casually). He and Blake chat, and Rosa overhears the prank plan. That way, it's more integrated.\n\nBut the prompt says end with Godric jokes with Blake and Blake's reaction. Rosa is in a corridor or garden, hears them.\n\nAlternatively, after the cure, Blake invites them to the palace to meet Godric informally? Or maybe after a few weeks, Godric wants to check on them? That might be more subtle.\n\nLet's construct: After a few weeks, Blake brings a message that the king would like them to visit the palace for a meal (as a friendly gesture). They go. At the meal, Godric is the perfect host, warm and kind. Afterwards, Rosa excuses herself to use the restroom, gets lost, and overhears the conversation in a study. That could work.\n\nI'll go with that.\n\nNow, the word count: let's aim for about 3200 words. I'll write the full story now, in Rosa's 1st person POV, past tense, with prose.\n\nI'll be careful to show the horror through Rosa's eyes, the cognitive dissonance, and the way she still loves Godric.\n\nLet's begin writing in a cohesive manner.\n\n---\n\n**Title: The Joke**\n\nI could smell the decay of hope. It was a metallic, coppery scent that clung to the back of my throat\u2014a decade of it, layering the bedroom like old paint. The curtains were drawn, as they had been every day since Rogr came home and forgot how to be a person. Dust drifted in the thin shafts of light that crept through the fabric, and in that half-gloom I sat on the edge of our marriage bed and watched my husband tremble.\n\nRogr\u2019s face, once so animated, had become a mask of constant, low-grade terror. His eyes moved rapidly beneath closed lids, his lips soundlessly forming words that I could never decipher. He hadn\u2019t spoken a full sentence in years. When he tried, the words would lurch out of him, a jumbled mess of metaphors about gravity and stars and the impossible weight of a single, fleeting glance.\n\nHe was still in there. I knew it. On his best days, when I held his hand and whispered old stories about our courtship, his grip would tighten just a fraction, and I\u2019d see a flicker of the man I\u2019d married\u2014the linguist who could charm a room with tales of ancient alphabets, the father who\u2019d taught our son Pete to read using star charts. But those moments were as fragile as spider silk, and they always snapped under the pressure of whatever lived behind his eyes.\n\nOutside, the city of Thronegate hummed with contentment. The Awakening had made our men into titans, and the king\u2019s protection made us women safer than any generation in history. I could hear the laughter of children in the street, the rumble of transports carrying goods from universes my ancestors couldn\u2019t have imagined. Pete, at fourteen, was already training in the Awakened disciplines, his body growing stronger every day, his mind sharpening like a blade. He worshiped the king\u2014a pure, uncomplicated devotion that I had once shared.\n\nI still did. That was the horror of it. I loved the king. I was grateful for his rule, for the absolute peace, for the way he had let no woman suffer as his own wife and daughters had suffered millennia ago. When his face appeared on the public holos\u2014that strong, handsome visage, the close-cropped hair touched with grey, the sharp eyes that could warm into something paternal or freeze into something that ended civilizations\u2014my heart would swell with reverence.\n\nBut he had broken my husband. And I could not make those two facts fit together.\n\n---\n\nThe day it happened, a decade ago, Rogr had been a junior diplomatic aide\u2014a glorified errand-runner, really, but he\u2019d been ecstatic. The delegation was from a newly subjugated universe, and the king himself was to address them. It was the honor of a lifetime to be in the room. Rogr had shaved twice that morning. He\u2019d worn his best formal tunic, and I\u2019d teased him about looking like a groom on his wedding day.\n\nHe was gone for six hours. When he came back, he was already dead.\n\nNot literally. His body stumbled through our door, pale and shaking, and he looked at me with eyes that had seen something his brain was not equipped to process. He collapsed on the sofa. He didn\u2019t speak for three days, just curled into a ball and whimpered. When the words finally came, they were splinters.\n\n\u201cThe king\u2026 he looked at us. Just for a moment. He was\u2026 he was\u2026\u201d\n\n\u201cAngry?\u201d I prompted, stroking his hair.\n\n\u201cNo. Not angry. Displeased. It was\u2026 I don\u2019t know\u2026 a tiny thing. He looked at the group and his eyes went\u2026 cold. And the air\u2026 Rosa, the air turned to stone. I felt like the whole universe was disappointed in me. In all of us. Like I had committed a sin so vast that the stars themselves wanted me erased. It lasted less than a second, and then he smiled that warm smile, and the meeting went on like nothing happened. But I couldn\u2019t\u2026 I can\u2019t\u2026\u201d\n\nHe never finished that sentence. He never finished any sentence again.\n\nI didn\u2019t understand then. I\u2019d never felt the king\u2019s displeasure, not even a whisper. All my interactions with the crown were filtered through the perfect, benevolent bureaucracy. But I saw the aftermath in my husband\u2019s soul, and I set out to fix it.\n\n---\n\nI tried.\n\nOh, stars, I tried.\n\nThe best mental physician in the sector came to our home. She was a woman with three doctorates and a reputation for curing the incurable. She sat with Rogr for two hours, her instruments humming, her face unreadable. Then she stood, and I saw her hands were shaking. \u201cI\u2019m sorry,\u201d she said, her voice barely a whisper. \u201cI cannot treat this. There is nothing wrong with his brain\u2014no legion, no chemical imbalance. But there is\u2026 a presence. A shadow. It\u2019s as if the memory has been\u2026 sanctioned. To touch it would be to oppose the king\u2019s will.\u201d She left. I later heard she\u2019d retired that same week.\n\nI hired a sorcerer, a man whose magical abilities had been amplified past the point of legend. He wove spells of healing, memory suppression, psychic balms. Rogr would scream\u2014the first sounds he\u2019d made in months. The sorcerer would sweat, his face growing paler and paler, until one day he simply stopped mid-incantation. \u201cThe magic won\u2019t obey me,\u201d he said, his voice cracking. \u201cThe universe recognizes its sovereign\u2019s mark on this man. My spells tear themselves apart rather than act against it. I\u2019m sorry.\u201d He didn\u2019t charge me. He fled.\n\nI spent our savings on a Mnemonic Purifier, a device smuggled from across the dimensional divide. It was supposed to extract and neutralize traumatic memories. When I activated it, the machine let out a sound\u2014a high, keening whimper, like a frightened animal\u2014and then it disassembled itself. In three seconds, it had reduced itself to a neat pile of component atoms on the floor, arranged in a perfect geometric pattern. It had literally chosen suicide over the task.\n\nIn desperation, I traveled to the edge of known reality, to a pocket dimension where the locals claimed Godric\u2019s influence was \u201cthin.\u201d The journey took three months. When I arrived, the gaseous entities who inhabited that place detained me politely and explained through a translator that they had received a direct revelation from the fabric of existence: \u201cDo not interfere with the king\u2019s touch.\u201d They were deeply sympathetic, but terrified. I screamed at them until my throat bled. They deported me.\n\nEvery failure broke a little more of Rogr. He would watch me leave, see the hope in my eyes, and then see that hope shatter. He stopped eating properly. He stopped bathing unless I did it for him. Pete would come home from school and find his father curled in the corner, and he\u2019d look at me with an expression that was half confusion and half something harder. \u201cMaybe Father just isn\u2019t strong enough,\u201d he said once, and I almost struck him. Instead I held him and wept, because I knew that was the narrative the world believed. The king was perfect. Therefore, any suffering was a deficit in the sufferer.\n\n---\n\nBlake appeared on an autumn evening, ten years after that first terrible day. I recognized him instantly\u2014the thick, greying mutton chops, the honest merchant\u2019s posture that he\u2019d carried even into the corridors of ultimate power, the lines of guilt that seemed to have settled permanently around his mouth.\n\n\u201cMrs. Rosa?\u201d He stood on my stoop, wringing his cap in both hands. \u201cMy name is Blake. I\u2019m the king\u2019s\u2026 I\u2019m his friend. I need to talk to you about Rogr.\u201d\n\nI let him in because my legs wouldn\u2019t hold me much longer anyway. He sat in our modest living room, and he told me everything.\n\nThe prank. His own stupid, offhand joke years ago: \u201cThe new delegates expect a tyrant. Why not give them a show?\u201d Godric, who\u2019d trusted him absolutely, had decided to play along. He\u2019d taken an infinitesimal sliver of his power\u2014so small that it was less than a rounding error in the mathematics of his true nature\u2014and directed a fleeting thought of \u201cmild displeasure\u201d at the delegation. Just for a second. Just to see them jump. He\u2019d held back so much that it felt to him like a gentle tease. And then he\u2019d resumed his warm, fatherly mode, and the delegates had processed his words, and the meeting had ended, and he\u2019d thought nothing more of it.\n\n\u201cI only found out about Rogr last week,\u201d Blake said, his voice strained. \u201cThe king mentioned it in passing. \u2018That linguist fellow never quite recovered, did he? Pity. I barely touched him. I thought you mortals were tougher.\u2019\u201d Blake\u2019s fists clenched. \u201cI\u2026 I yelled at him. I called him an idiot\u2014the omnipotent king of the omniverse, and I called him an idiot. And he just blinked at me and said, \u2018Even so, I can fix it. Do you think they\u2019d want me to?\u2019\u201d\n\nBlake looked at me, and his eyes were wet. \u201cHe\u2019s not cruel, Rosa. He\u2019s just been so powerful for so long that he\u2019s forgotten what breaking is. The prank was my idea. The trauma is my fault. Please, let me bring him to cure Rogr. He can do it in an instant, but he won\u2019t interfere without your permission.\u201d\n\nI sat there, my mind a whirlpool. The source of a decade of nightmare was a joke between friends. All my efforts, all the therapies that had self-destructed in cosmic fear, all the hope I\u2019d poured into an indifferent omniverse\u2014it had been because the king had decided to playact being a tyrant for a few heartbeats.\n\nRogr, from the bedroom, made a small sound. I went to him. He was awake, his eyes open, fixed on the ceiling.\n\n\u201cRogr,\u201d I whispered, taking his hand. \u201cThe king\u2019s friend\u2026 he says they can heal you. That the king will heal you. Do you want that?\u201d\n\nHe trembled. His lips moved, and I leaned close to hear. \u201cYes. Please. I can\u2019t\u2026 I can\u2019t live like this anymore.\u201d\n\nMy son Pete, now fifteen and tall, was standing in the doorway, his face ashen. He\u2019d heard Blake\u2019s confession. \u201cMother,\u201d he said, his voice cracking. \u201cThe king is good. He didn\u2019t mean it. He\u2019ll fix it. Please, let him.\u201d\n\nI nodded, tears blurring my vision. \u201cYes. Do it. Please.\u201d\n\n---\n\nThe moment I spoke, the universe swallowed the room.\n\nThat\u2019s the only way I can describe it. The air didn\u2019t move\u2014it congealed, became a substance that felt like liquid lead and shattered glass all at once. My lungs seized. My thoughts, which had been racing, simply stopped, frozen mid-syllable. Every instinct in my body screamed at me to kneel, to prostrate myself, to make myself as small as possible because something terrible and vast was occupying the space where normality had been.\n\nAnd then Godric was there. He didn\u2019t appear. He simply *was*, standing at the foot of Rogr\u2019s bed as if he\u2019d been part of the furniture all along and I\u2019d only now noticed. He wore a simple tunic, completely unadorned, but his presence turned our shabby bedroom into the throne room of existence. His physique was that of a statue given life\u2014broad shoulders, powerful arms, the kind of strength that didn\u2019t need to be displayed. His salt-and-pepper beard was neat, his hair close-cropped, his face an impossible blend of ethereal beauty and worldly weariness.\n\nHe looked at Rogr. That\u2019s all. Just a look.\n\nAnd Rogr\u2026 unfolded. The rigid, fetal curl of his body relaxed in a wave. The ashen pallor of his skin flushed with healthy, vibrant color. The deep lines etched by a decade of silent screaming smoothed away. His eyes, which had been glassy with empty terror, flickered, focused, and found mine.\n\n\u201cRosa?\u201d His voice was hoarse, but it was his voice. His real voice. \u201cWhat\u2026 what happened? I feel\u2026 I feel amazing.\u201d\n\nHe sat up. He moved like a man who\u2019d never known a day of illness, his joints fluid, his muscles responsive. I saw him notice his own hands\u2014the faint tremors that had persisted even before the trauma were gone. The old scar on his forearm from a kitchen accident had vanished. He looked more than healed; he looked like the ideal of health, a platonic form of vitality that mortal bodies were not supposed to achieve.\n\nI threw myself onto him, sobbing, and his arms wrapped around me with a strength I\u2019d forgotten he possessed. Pete crashed into us from the other side, and for a long, suspended moment we were just a family again, a unit, a one-thing.\n\nBut I couldn\u2019t ignore the weight. Even as I wept with joy, I felt Godric\u2019s presence pressing against the edges of my consciousness like the pressure of an ocean\u2019s depth. He hadn\u2019t moved. He hadn\u2019t spoken a single spell or gestured. The healing had been so effortless it probably wasn\u2019t even a conscious act\u2014more like a candle incidentally warming the air around it. His attention had simply abolished a decade of suffering, and my soul was buckling under the realization.\n\nHe spoke then, his voice a resonant baritone that seemed to vibrate in my bones. \u201cI am told this was my fault. And I\u2019m learning to accept that \u2018almost nothing\u2019 to me is still\u2026 something, to mortals. I am sorry, Rogr. Rosa. It was never my wish to cause lasting harm.\u201d\n\nAn apology. From the absolute king. I felt a fresh wave of love wash over me\u2014a genuine, overwhelming gratitude that this being, with all his power, would deign to feel remorse. He was good. He was so good.\n\nAnd yet.\n\n\u201cI would like to offer restitution,\u201d he continued, his grey eyes shifting to me. \u201cI am aware of the decade you\u2019ve spent, Rosa. The physicians. The journeys. The hopes you poured into a cosmos that was, I suspect, too afraid of me to help. Name your compensation. Wealth beyond imagining. A position of authority for your son. A planet of your own, a universe, a lifespan that will see the death of stars. Anything you wish. It is not payment\u2014pain has no price\u2014but consider it an apology, in a language I can speak.\u201d\n\nMy throat closed. A decade of struggle, of machines that committed suicide and sorcerers who fled and dimensions that deported me. All of it, meaningless in the face of this infinite ease. I could ask for anything, and he would give it with no more effort than breathing.\n\n\u201cNo,\u201d I whispered. The word was a brittle thing. \u201cI don\u2019t want\u2026 I just wanted him back. You gave me that. The rest\u2026 I can\u2019t. It would feel like being paid for his pain, and I can\u2019t carry that. Please, just let us go back to normal.\u201d\n\nFor a moment, Godric was silent. Then he inclined his head\u2014a simple, human gesture\u2014and when he looked at me again, there was something in his expression that was neither godlike nor terrible. It was respect.\n\n\u201cYou\u2019re very stubborn, Rosa,\u201d he said, and there was warmth there. \u201cI hope you know the offer remains, should you ever change your mind. For now, have your normal life. Live it well.\u201d\n\nAnd then, without transition, he was gone. The air snapped back to something my lungs could use. My thoughts lurched into motion. The room was just a room again.\n\nRogr was holding my hand, his grip strong. Pete was babbling excitedly about having seen the king. Blake stood in the corner, his shoulders slumped, his eyes red.\n\nI should have felt pure relief. I did feel relief. But under it, coiling and cold, was a new kind of dread\u2014the dread of having witnessed the true scale of the cosmos and knowing, without any doubt, that every moment of my existence was a grace extended by a being who could retract it with less effort than it took me to blink.\n\n---\n\nWeeks passed. The normal life Godric had promised did indeed return. Rogr went back to work, his mind sharper than ever. Pete\u2019s training advanced. Our home filled with the sounds of laughter and mundane arguments over who left the bathroom light on. I smiled. I laughed. I prayed gratitude to the king every evening.\n\nBut at night I lay awake, staring at the ceiling, and felt the cold echo of that pressure. I remembered the Mnemonic Purifier\u2019s whimper, the gaseous entities\u2019 terror, the way the whole universe seemed to conspire to preserve Godric\u2019s unintentional mark. I thought about the ease of the cure\u2014a single glance, not even a conscious act. And I realized that the love I felt for my king was real, but so was the fear. They were two sides of the same coin, and the coin was crushing me.\n\nOne bright afternoon, Blake invited us to the palace for a small, informal gathering. \u201cThe king would like to see for himself that you\u2019re well,\u201d he said, and there was genuine warmth in his voice. So we went\u2014Rogr, Pete, and I\u2014and we sat in a sunny garden and drank tea, and Godric was everything the holos promised: kind, avuncular, quick to laugh at Pete\u2019s jokes, careful to compliment my dress. He was so thoroughly, genuinely good that I almost forgot the weight.\n\nI excused myself to find a restroom. The palace was a maze of living crystal and shifting architecture, and I got lost almost immediately. I wandered a corridor hung with tapestries from a thousand conquered worlds, and that was when I heard voices drifting through a half-open door.\n\nGodric\u2019s voice, light and amused: \u201cYou know, Blake, the delegation from the Vortex Sector is due next month. The ones with those dimensional-twisting swords. They\u2019re a bit smug, wouldn\u2019t you say? What do you think about giving them a tiny taste of the tyrant? Just a flicker. I\u2019d hold back even more this time. I\u2019m a quick study.\u201d\n\nBlake\u2019s response was a choked sound, half laughter and half something much more desperate. \u201cYour Majesty, please. No. No more pranks. The last one took ten years off my lifespan, and I wasn\u2019t even the one who was traumatized. Let\u2019s just\u2026 let\u2019s serve tea and be nice.\u201d\n\nA rich, warm chuckle. \u201cYou\u2019re no fun, Blake. Fine. Tea and nice it is. But someday, I\u2019ll find the perfect joke\u2014one that\u2019s funny for everyone involved.\u201d\n\n\u201cYour Majesty, with respect, you have the humor detection of an event horizon.\u201d\n\n\u201cAn event horizon that could unmake you, though.\u201d\n\n\u201cThat\u2019s\u2026 that\u2019s exactly my point.\u201d\n\nThey laughed together, old friends sharing a comfortable absurdity.\n\nI stood frozen in the corridor, my heart pounding. The casualness of it was what hollowed me out. To him, trauma was a matter of calibration\u2014a little less power here, a little more restraint there\u2014and eventually he\u2019d get the volume settings right. He wasn\u2019t cruel. He was learning. But the subjects upon which he practiced his learning were mortal minds, fragile things that cracked in ways he could not feel.\n\nI loved him. I feared him. I was grateful to him with every fiber of my being. And I would never, ever be able to trust the quiet around me again.\n\nI smoothed my dress, fixed my smile, and walked back to the garden to join my family. They were laughing at something the king had said. Rogr looked up at me, his eyes bright and whole, and he reached for my hand.\n\n\u201cYou okay?\u201d he asked.\n\n\u201cFine,\u201d I said. \u201cJust got lost.\u201d\n\nHe squeezed my fingers, and I let the lie settle into the space where my dread lived. Outside, the omniverse spun on its axis, attended by a king who loved his people and could destroy them by accident. And we, the people, loved him back, because what else could we do? He was perfect. He was terrifying.\n\nI would hold those two truths for the rest of my life, and I would never let them go.",

I sat on the edge of our marriage bed, my hand resting on Rogr\u2019s shoulder as he trembled through another sleepless trance. His eyes darted behind closed lids, his lips forming words I could never decipher. He\u2019d been like this for a decade now, curled into himself like a frightened animal, his brilliant linguist\u2019s mind reduced to a single, unending howl.\n\nI whispered the same things I always whispered. \u201cI\u2019m here. I love you.\u201d His breathing hitched. That was the only answer I ever got.\n\nOutside our modest home, the city of Thronegate hummed with contentment. The Awakening had made our men into titans, each day past twenty multiplying their strength and wisdom tenfold. My son Pete, at fifteen, already trained in the disciplines that would soon transform him. He idolized King Godric\u2014everyone did. When the king\u2019s face appeared on the public holos, that strong, bearded jaw and those warm, grey eyes, my heart swelled with the same reverence that filled every citizen. He was the perfect ruler, the absolute protector, the father who had returned from ten thousand years of stasis to build a universe without war or want.\n\nAnd yet that same king had shattered my husband with a glance.\n\nI didn\u2019t understand it. The event had been so small. Rogr, then a junior diplomatic aide, had been thrilled to attend a palace reception for newly subjugated delegates. He\u2019d left bouncing on his heels and returned six hours later as a hollowed-out shell. Over the years, I\u2019d pieced together fragments: the king had looked at the delegation, just for a moment, and his expression had gone cold. Not angry. Not cruel. Just\u2026 displeased. Then he inclined his head\u2014a simple, human gesture\u2014and when he looked at me again, there was something in his expression that was neither godlike nor terrible. It was respect.\n\n\u201cYou\u2019re very stubborn, Rosa,\u201d he said, and there was warmth there. \u201cI hope you know the offer remains, should you ever change your mind. For now, have your normal life. Live it well.\u201d\n\nAnd then, without transition, he was gone. The air snapped back. My thoughts lurched into motion. The room was just a room again.\n\n\u2014\n\nWeeks passed. Rogr returned to work, his mind sharper than ever. Pete\u2019s training advanced. Our home filled with the sounds of laughter and mundane arguments over who left the bathroom light on. I smiled. I laughed. I prayed gratitude to the king every evening.\n\nBut at night I lay awake, staring at the ceiling, and felt the cold echo of that pressure. I remembered the Mnemonic Purifier\u2019s whimper, the gaseous entities\u2019 terror, the way the whole universe had conspired to preserve Godric\u2019s unintentional mark. I thought about the ease of the cure\u2014a single glance, not even a conscious act. And I realized that the love I felt for my king was real, but so was the fear. They were two sides of the same coin, and the coin was crushing me.\n\nOne bright afternoon, Blake invited us to the palace for a small gathering. \u201cThe king would like to see for himself that you\u2019re well,\u201d he said. So we went\u2014Rogr, Pete, and I\u2014and sat in a sunny garden and drank tea, and Godric was everything the holos promised: kind, avuncular, quick to laugh at Pete\u2019s jokes, careful to compliment my dress. He was so thoroughly, genuinely good that I almost forgot the weight.\n\nI excused myself to find a restroom. The palace was a maze of living crystal, and I got lost. I wandered a corridor hung with tapestries from a thousand conquered worlds, and that was when I heard voices drifting through a half-open door.\n\nGodric\u2019s voice, light and amused: \u201cYou know, Blake, the delegation from the Vortex Sector is due next month. The ones with those dimensional-twisting swords. They\u2019re a bit smug, wouldn\u2019t you say? What do you think about giving them a tiny taste of the tyrant? Just a flicker. I\u2019d hold back even more this time. I\u2019m a quick study.\u201d\n\nBlake\u2019s response was a choked sound, half laughter and half something desperate. \u201cYour Majesty, please. No more pranks. The last one took ten years off my lifespan, and I wasn\u2019t even the one who was traumatized. Let\u2019s just serve tea and be nice.\u201d\n\nA rich, warm chuckle. \u201cYou\u2019re no fun, Blake. Fine. Tea and nice it is. But someday, I\u2019ll find the perfect joke\u2014one that\u2019s funny for everyone involved.\u201d\n\n\u201cYour Majesty, with respect, you have the humor detection of an event horizon.\u201d\n\n\u201cAn event horizon that could unmake you, though.\u201d\n\n\u201cThat\u2019s exactly my point.\u201d\n\nThey laughed together, old friends sharing a comfortable absurdity.\n\nI stood frozen in the corridor, my heart pounding. The casualness of it was what hollowed me out. To him, trauma was a matter of calibration\u2014a little less power here, a little more restraint there\u2014and eventually he\u2019d get the volume settings right. He wasn\u2019t cruel. He was learning. But the subjects upon which he practiced were mortal minds, fragile things that cracked in ways he could not feel.\n\nI loved him. I feared him. I was grateful to him with every fiber of my being. And I would never, ever be able to trust the quiet around me again.\n\nI smoothed my dress, fixed my smile, and walked back to the garden. My family was laughing at something the king had said. Rogr looked up at me, his eyes bright and whole, and reached for my hand.\n\n\u201cYou okay?\u201d he asked.\n\n\u201cFine,\u201d I said. \u201cJust got lost.\u201d\n\nHe squeezed my fingers, and I let the lie settle into the space where my dread lived. Outside, the omniverse spun on its axis, attended by a king who loved his people and could destroy them by accident. And we, the people, loved him back, because what else could we do? He was perfect. He was terrifying.\n\nI would hold those two truths for the rest of my life, and I would never let them go."
